## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity) and optional explicit time dependence t, matching second-order ODE models of (non)linear harmonic oscillators including damping and external forcing. Common structures express dv_dt as sums of restoring forces in x, damping terms in v, and possibly time-periodic drives in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped, unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x (small-amplitude restoring force approximation)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped spring-mass with linear drag)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear resonance)
- Quadratic stiffness (asymmetric restoring): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (broken-symmetry oscillator)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations with amplitude limiting)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent negative damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (self-oscillation via nonlinear friction)
- Pendulum (small-to-moderate angles): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (nonlinear restoring from gravity; x as angle)
- Potential-derived force (energy landscape): dv_dt = -c0 * (c1 * x + c2 * x**3 + c3 * x**5) + c4 * v (polynomial potential gradient approximation)
- Saturating restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * tanh(c1 * x) + c2 * v (bounded restoring force / softening at large |x|)
- Coulomb + viscous friction (stick-slip surrogate): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (smooth dry-friction approximation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force → dv_dt mainly depends on x (often odd in x), with weak/no dependence on v; indicates near-energy-conserving motion.
- Linear damping → additive term proportional to v; produces exponential decay of oscillation amplitude in time without changing equilibrium position.
- Nonlinear stiffness (x**3, x**5, sin(c*x), tanh(c*x)) → amplitude-dependent frequency (backbone curve) and potential multistability/hysteresis under drive.
- Self-excitation/amplitude regulation → terms like (c0 - c1 * x**2) * v or (c0 - c1 * v**2) * v; negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude leads to limit cycles.
- External periodic forcing → additive sin/cos(c*t) terms; produces entrainment, resonance peaks, and possibly quasiperiodicity/chaos when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric modulation → x multiplied by periodic function of t; instability tongues and growth near twice the natural frequency.
- Quadratic drag / aerodynamic damping → v * Abs(v) (or v**3) terms; stronger dissipation at high speeds, sharper decay for large-amplitude motion.
- Dry friction signatures → tanh(c*v) (smooth sign) terms; yields piecewise-like acceleration near v≈0 and can induce stick-slip behavior.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO38)
============================================================
GT: -beta*sin(v) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the ground truth:

**GT:** `-0.194830767863936*v*(1 - x**2) - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

Expanding: `0.194830767863936*v*x**2 - 0.194830767863936*v - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v*x**2` (coefficient ≈ 0.1948)
2. `v` (coefficient ≈ -0.1948)
3. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` (coefficient ≈ -3.0492)
4. `sin(v)` (coefficient ≈ -0.1430)

Key challenges:
- `x*exp(-Abs(x))` is a specific function that's not a polynomial, not `tanh`, etc.
- `sin(v)` is a specific nonlinear function of v

Let me analyze the candidates systematically. Most candidates use combinations of polynomials in x, `tanh(x)`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v**3`, `x**n`, `Max(0,...)`, etc. None of these can exactly reproduce `x*exp(-Abs(x))` or `sin(v)`.

**For `x*exp(-Abs(x))`:** This function has a specific shape - it peaks near x=±1 and decays exponentially. No finite polynomial in x can match this. `tanh` functions are bounded sigmoids, not the same. `x/(c*Abs(x)+1)` is a rational function, not equivalent.

**For `sin(v)`:** This is periodic and bounded. No polynomial in v (`v`, `v**3`, `v**5`, `v*Abs(v)`) can match it exactly. `tanh(v)` is not periodic, so it can't match `sin(v)` either.

Let me check if any candidate has both `x*exp(-Abs(x))` (or equivalent) AND `sin(v)` (or equivalent) as basis functions:

Going through all 50 candidates:
- None contain `exp(-Abs(x))` or `exp(-|x|)` terms
- None contain `sin(v)` terms
- Some contain `sin(c*t + c)` which depends on t, not v
- Some contain `tanh(c*v)` (Candidate 5) but tanh ≠ sin

Since `x*exp(-Abs(x))` cannot be exactly represented by any finite combination of polynomials, `tanh`, `Max`, rational functions, or other basis functions present in the candidates, and `sin(v)` cannot be exactly represented by polynomials in v or `tanh(v)`, **none of the candidates can match the GT**.

Let me double-check a few promising ones:
- **Candidates with `tanh`:** `tanh` approaches ±1 asymptotically while `x*exp(-Abs(x))` approaches 0. No combination of `tanh` functions equals `x*exp(-Abs(x))`.
- **Candidates with `x/(c*Abs(x)+1)`** (14, 15, 29, 34, 35): This is a rational approximation but NOT exact. For large x, `x/(c|x|+1) → 1/c` while `x*exp(-|x|) → 0`.
- **Candidates with `Max(0, c + Abs(x))`** (20, 21, 26, 27, 36-40): These are piecewise linear, not exponentially decaying.
